# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
y ^OcMg80qw

x ^mtsKw7di

How do you fit a curve that looks like this set of features? ^G5YPTGdR

We solve this with a algorithm called ^TDfPiZAE

Locally weighted regression ^nPtm0feX

"Parametric" learning algorithm:
    Fit fixed set of parameters (θ ) to data.
"Non-parametric" learning algorithm:
    Amount of data/parameters you need to keep grows       (linearly) with size of data. May not be good if you have large amounts of data. ^VPh5cL3o

i ^wNCRyqVf

To evaluate h at a certain x: ^nW1ja9FB

Linear regression: 
Fit θ to minimize ^6v4oCgse

Return θ x ^75ZKXnrD

T ^I1iBUFFW

x ^Dv6yAhaP

Locally weighted regression:
Fit θ to minimize ^7HXMWC0M

x ^j9Eb2o7O

x ^ByMmR6Yj

Where w  is a "weight" function. ^9Jz7AHjZ

If  ^u2xUdkuW

(i) ^wXTC5cJO

is small, w ^lgMTMO4M

(i) ^qJXhj0EK

1. ^OR1rVvjK

location where you want to make the prediction ^cHzCT4BW

input x for ith training example ^CzdxisCL

So w  is a weighting function that's a value between 0 and 1 that tells you how much you should pay attention to the values of        
when fitting some function. ^n5I8Wk7K

(i) ^K8yLx80t

If  ^MejHIqLT

is large, w ^R6HKvmzb

(i) ^OddNIx3V

0. ^93RoqjnP

if they are very far away ^ZXUblBwR

The examples far away are multiplied by 0, so the net effect of this is that it sums only examples that are close to the value of x where you want to make a prediction. ^MnR7rlMJ

How big a neighborhood (how fat the bell curve) should you look in order to the decide the neighbors points to use to fit your local straight line? ^9Tc6Vy00

x ^34TkwJnz

weights ^b434Zl64

τ ^wAXteb3Z

τ = "bandwidth" ^5Vz2zyZr

τ ^D7hXvg98

The value of τ decides how many nearby examples to use to fit the straight line. ^rMoVSxSu

You should tend to use locally weighted regression when you have a relatively low dimensional data set (number of features is not too big, 2,3,4), you have a lot of data (hundreds or thousands of examples) and don't wanna think about what features to use. ^LKHcec11
